## Page 2

<span style="font-family:'Arial';font-size:8.00pt;color:#a3a3a3">The Linux Memory Manager (Early Access) © 2025 by Lorenzo Stoakes</span>

<span style="font-family:'DogmaOT-Bold';font-size:16.00pt;font-weight:bold;color:#231f20">NO S TA RCH PR E S S </span>
<span style="font-family:'DogmaOT-Bold';font-size:16.00pt;font-weight:bold;color:#231f20">E A R LY  ACCE S S  PROG R A M: </span>
<span style="font-family:'DogmaOT-Bold';font-size:16.00pt;font-weight:bold;color:#231f20">F E E DBACK W E L COM E !</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleStd-Roman';font-size:10.00pt;color:#231f20">The Early Access program lets you read significant portions of an </span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleStd-Roman';font-size:10.00pt;color:#231f20">upcoming book while it’s still in the editing and production phases, so you </span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleStd-Roman';font-size:10.00pt;color:#231f20">may come across errors or other issues you want to comment on. But while </span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleStd-Roman';font-size:10.00pt;color:#231f20">we sincerely appreciate your feedback during a book’s EA phase, please use </span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleStd-Roman';font-size:10.00pt;color:#231f20">your best dis-cretion when deciding what to report. </span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleStd-Roman';font-size:10.00pt;color:#231f20">At the EA stage, we’re most interested in feedback related to content—</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleStd-Roman';font-size:10.00pt;color:#231f20">general comments to the writer, technical errors, versioning concerns, or </span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleStd-Roman';font-size:10.00pt;color:#231f20">other high-level issues and observations. As these titles are still in draft </span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleStd-Roman';font-size:10.00pt;color:#231f20">form, we already know there may be typos, grammatical mistakes, miss-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleStd-Roman';font-size:10.00pt;color:#231f20">ing images or captions, layout issues, and instances of placeholder text. No </span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleStd-Roman';font-size:10.00pt;color:#231f20">need to report these—they will all be corrected later, during the copyedit-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleStd-Roman';font-size:10.00pt;color:#231f20">ing, proofreading, and typesetting processes. Please note that any online </span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleStd-Roman';font-size:10.00pt;color:#231f20">resources may not be available until the book is complete. </span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleStd-Roman';font-size:10.00pt;color:#231f20">If you encounter any errors (“errata”) you’d like to report, please fill out </span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleStd-Roman';font-size:10.00pt;color:#231f20">this </span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleStd-Bold';font-size:10.00pt;font-weight:bold;color:#ed1c24">Google form</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleStd-Roman';font-size:10.00pt;color:#231f20"> so we can review your comments.</span>

## Page 16

<span style="font-family:'Arial';font-size:8.00pt;color:#a3a3a3">The Linux Memory Manager (Early Access) © 2025 by Lorenzo Stoakes</span>

<span style="font-family:'Futura-Bold';font-size:11.95pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">1.1</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura-Bold';font-size:11.95pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">Approach</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Many kernel books take the approach of providing an overview and then</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">hand-waving away details, that is a top-down approach..</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">The key motivating philosophy of the Linux Memory Manager was to do</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">entirely the opposite—explore each part of the memory management sub-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">system starting with basic principles, and then work from the bottom-up to</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">form a broader understanding of the topic at hand.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Within the kernel there can be no better source of truth than the source</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">code itself, so we explore kernel functionality by exploring its code, which is</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">reproduced in extensive snippets.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">In effect, this book tries to combine a source commentary with in depth</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">analysis of concepts explored in both extensive discussions of the concepts</span>

<span style="font-family:'Futura-CondensedBold';font-size:119.55pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">1</span>
<span style="font-family:'DogmaBold';font-size:15.94pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">INT ROD UCTI ON</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:13.95pt;color:#000000">The memory management subsystem is arguably the</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:13.95pt;color:#000000">core of the Linux kernel, forming the foundation</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:13.95pt;color:#000000">upon which the rest of the kernel and all of userspace</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:13.95pt;color:#000000">operates. Despite its fundamental nature, it is surpris-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:13.95pt;color:#000000">ingly complicated and intricate.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">The Linux Memory Manager explores the Linux kernel’s memory man-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">agement subsystem in detail. In this chapter we will explore the approach</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">taken, who the book is aimed it,</span>

---

## Page 17

<span style="font-family:'Arial';font-size:8.00pt;color:#a3a3a3">The Linux Memory Manager (Early Access) © 2025 by Lorenzo Stoakes</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">at hand along side a large number of diagrams which aim to put each con-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">cept into perspective.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">As the kernel is constantly evolving and this book necessarily must target</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">a static kernel version, the intent is that by taking this approach, not only</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">will the reader acquire understanding of fundamentals which are unlikely to</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">change, but more importantly develop their skills at exploring kernel source</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">so that they can adapt and update their knowledge to the latest version of</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">the code.</span>

<span style="font-family:'Futura-Bold';font-size:11.95pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">1.2</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura-Bold';font-size:11.95pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">Who Is This Book For?</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">This book is aimed at developers who already have some fundamental un-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">derstanding of the C programming language and operating system basics,</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">and have an interest in exploring under the hood to see how Linux manages</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">memory in as much detail as they may want to do so.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">This spans from that most wonderful of things—a genuinely curious</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">(perhaps aspiring?) kernel hacker to a professional kernel developer, either</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">working with or making use of the memory management subsystem.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">The intent is to bring out the hidden tribal knowledge within this code-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">base as much as possible and in the spirit of open source software make it</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">more widely available to curious hackers all over the world!</span>

<span style="font-family:'Futura-Bold';font-size:11.95pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">1.3</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura-Bold';font-size:11.95pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">Book Overview</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Bold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">Chapter 7: The Reverse Mapping</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> A detailed look at how the kernel maps</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">raw physical pages of userland memory back to the abstract VMA repre-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">sentation, in addition to how this is used to free memory.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Bold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">Chapter 8: Manipulating Userland Memory</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> A detailed examination of how</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">the kernel accesses userland memory. Also a brief look at how memory</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">ranges can be manipulated by</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> madvise()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">.</span>

<span style="font-family:'Futura-CondensedBold';font-size:8.97pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">2</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura';font-size:5.98pt;color:#000000">Chapter 1</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Bold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">Chapter 1: Introduction</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> A description of the contents of the book.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Bold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">Chapter 2: Physical Memory</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> A description of how a system’s memory is</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">managed on its most fundamental level—the allocation of its physically</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">installed RAM.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Bold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">Chapter 3: Virtual Memory</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> The why, what and how, page tables, page ta-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">ble flags, page table sizes, virtual memory layout, direct mapping, ker-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">nel/userland split and a detailed description of vmalloc().</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Bold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">Chapter 4: Process Memory</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> An overview of how userland memory is</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">structured—</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">mm_struct</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">, Process VMAs, Copy-on-Write and more.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Bold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">Chapter 5: Memory Mapping</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> A description of how memory mapping is</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">performed within the kernel -</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> mmap</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">,</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> brk</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> (used by</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> malloc()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">) and how map-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">pings (via VMAs) are split/merged.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Bold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">Chapter 6: Page Faults</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> A detailed examination of how page faults are han-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">dled and propagated within the kernel.</span>

## Page 18

<span style="font-family:'Arial';font-size:8.00pt;color:#a3a3a3">The Linux Memory Manager (Early Access) © 2025 by Lorenzo Stoakes</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Bold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">Chapter 9: The Page Cache</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> A detailed look into the page cache, how it in-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">teracts with the Linux virtual file system, read-ahead, read-behind and</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">generally a very focused discussion of how the memory subsystem inter-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">acts with VFS.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Bold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">Chapter 10: Writeback</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> A description of how writeback proceeds both orig-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">inating from write() operations and memory-mapped files, how dirty</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">data is tracked, how synchronisation functions within the kernel and</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">how dirty throttling is applied.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Bold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">Chapter 11: Reclaim and Memory Pressure</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> A detailed explanation of how</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">reclaim operations, what direct and indirect reclaim are, how it interacts</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">with demand paging, higher order page starvation, etc.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Bold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">Chapter 12: Swap Memory</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> A detailed description of how the swap oper-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">ations in the kernel and how pages are paged out and paged back in</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">again.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Bold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">Chapter 13: The Out of Memory (OOM) Killer</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> A deep dive into how it</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">works, how to tune it, the what, why and how.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Bold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">Chapter 14: Practical Memory Management</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> A brief overview of practical</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">memory management techniques - procfs interfaces, tuneables, decod-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">ing out of memory reports and more. Generally a practical ’how to’ for</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">sysadmins/developers.</span>

## Page 19

---

## Page 20

<span style="font-family:'Arial';font-size:8.00pt;color:#a3a3a3">The Linux Memory Manager (Early Access) © 2025 by Lorenzo Stoakes</span>

<span style="font-family:'Futura-CondensedBold';font-size:119.55pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">2</span>

<span style="font-family:'DogmaBold';font-size:15.94pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">PHY SIC AL MEM ORY</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:13.95pt;color:#000000">Physical memory describes all of the memory on a sys-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:13.95pt;color:#000000">tem which can be addressed arbitrarily by at least one</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:13.95pt;color:#000000">core. Typically this will be in the form of RAM mod-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:13.95pt;color:#000000">ules but could include other forms of random-access</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:13.95pt;color:#000000">stores. Over the course of this chapter we will explore</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:13.95pt;color:#000000">how the kernel manages, allocates and abstracts this</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:13.95pt;color:#000000">resource.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Physical addresses</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> tell the CPU where to find a particular byte of memory.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">For example, DRAM stores each individual byte on a specific row and col-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">umn in a specific array known as a bank, accessed by a specific channel on a</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">DIMM stored in a specific slot. The physical address encodes all of this infor-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">mation.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Within the kernel, physical addresses are assigned the</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> phys_addr_t</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> type</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">which is equal to the word size, e.g. for a 64-bit system this is simply an un-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">signed 64-bit integer.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">If we were to try to manage every byte of memory individually the over-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">head associated with trying to keep a track of it would exceed the amount</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">of available memory in the system. This is obviously intractable so we have</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">to compromise and subdivide memory into aggregate blocks, which we call</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">pages</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">.</span>

---

## Page 21

<span style="font-family:'Arial';font-size:8.00pt;color:#a3a3a3">The Linux Memory Manager (Early Access) © 2025 by Lorenzo Stoakes</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">The</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> base page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> size of an architecture is the hardware-configured mini-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">mum supported page size and thus the fundamental unit of memory. For</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">x86-64 this is 2</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:6.97pt;color:#000000">12</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> </span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">or 4,096 bytes, for arm64 and other architectures how-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">ever this can vary. In the Linux kernel the base page size is defined to be</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">PAGE_SIZE</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> bytes (This is architecture-specific and so declared in the appropri-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">ate</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> arch/</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> header file).</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">We subdivide pages further into</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> nodes</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> zones</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">. Let’s examine what each</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">of these mean:</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Large server boxes may support more than once CPU socket with some</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">memory modules attached to one CPU, some attached to another and so</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">on, with some slow means of interconnect between remote blocks of mem-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">ory.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Systems with memory arranged in this configuration are said to have a</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Non-Uniform Memory Access (</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">NUMA</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">) memory architecture.</span>

<span style="font-family:'DogmaBold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#ffffff">N O T E</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">In addition, systems may even have blocks of memory that don’t have a CPU asso-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">ciated with them and are slow for any core to access, or are attached to a CPU with</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">locality to other memory also attached to the same CPU, but possess other characteris-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">tics which reduces the speed of access to them.</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Even single-CPU systems on modern hardware are typically treated as</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">NUMA, only with a single NUMA node defined which owns all physical</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">memory.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">In order for the kernel to take these heterogeneous memory blocks into</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">account it subdivides them into physically contiguous domains known as</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">nodes</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">, with each page of physical memory belonging to one and only one</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">node.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Within each node memory is further divided based on physical address</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">ranges</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> into areas known as</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> zones</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">. This is either because that range of mem-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">ory naturally possesses an important characteristic or because a range of</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">memory has been arbitrarily assigned to a particular purpose. Zones overlap</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">nodes.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">It is important to note that for a modern system which has NUMA en-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">abled, physical memory allocation will always be parameterised by node and</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">zone (even if they may have been automatically determined by a function</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">higher up the call stack).</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">In order to efficiently allocate memory the kernel allocates memory in</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">power-of-two numbers of base pages at a time with the</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> order</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> of an allocated</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">page being equal this power-of-two e.g. an order-3 allocation consists of 2</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:6.97pt;color:#000000">3</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> </span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">=</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">8 base pages of memory.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Each base page of physical memory has metadata associated with it</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">which is stored in</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> objects, with aggregate blocks of 1 or more</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">base pages represented as a</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct folio</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> object.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">For convenience we define the useful notion of a</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> Page Frame Number</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">(PFN) which is simply the physical address divided by the page size, in other</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">words if you were to conceive of physical pages as elements in an array, the</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">PFN is the index of a page in that array.</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PFN_PHYS()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PHYS_PFN()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> are used to</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">convert between the two.</span>

<span style="font-family:'Futura-CondensedBold';font-size:8.97pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">6</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura';font-size:5.98pt;color:#000000">Chapter 2</span>

---

## Page 22

<span style="font-family:'Arial';font-size:8.00pt;color:#a3a3a3">The Linux Memory Manager (Early Access) © 2025 by Lorenzo Stoakes</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Memory is further divided into</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> page blocks</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> (the order of which is defined</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">by</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> pageblock_order</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">, 9 on x86-64, i.e. 512 pages). These are the smallest num-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">ber of pages which can have a</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> migrate type</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> applied to them. A migrate type</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">determines whether pages can be</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> migrated</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> i.e. moved around, described by</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">enum migratetype</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">. More on this later.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Let’s examine an example physical memory layout in Figure 2-1.</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:6.97pt;color:#000000">Node 2</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:6.97pt;color:#000000">Zone C</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:6.97pt;color:#000000">Node 1</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:6.97pt;color:#000000">Page</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:6.97pt;color:#000000">Page</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:6.97pt;color:#000000">block</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:6.97pt;color:#000000">Zone B</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:6.97pt;color:#000000">Node 0</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:6.97pt;color:#000000">Zone A</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:6.97pt;color:#000000">Physical</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:6.97pt;color:#000000">address</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">0</span>

<span style="font-family:'Futura-BookOblique';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000">Figure 2-1: Example physical memory layout</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">The line represents physical memory from zero to the maximum avail-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">able to the system.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Note that this diagram excludes memory</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> holes</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">, (blocks of physical mem-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">ory inaccessible for use as ordinary memory—either empty, reserved or used</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">by devices) for simplicity.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Each node and zone subdivides the physical address space into contigu-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">ous blocks of memory, with zones overlapping nodes. Each node and zone</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">are page-aligned so base pages belong definitely to a node and a zone.</span>

<span style="font-family:'Futura';font-size:5.98pt;color:#000000">Physical Memory</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura-CondensedBold';font-size:8.97pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">7</span>

---

## Page 23

<span style="font-family:'Arial';font-size:8.00pt;color:#a3a3a3">The Linux Memory Manager (Early Access) © 2025 by Lorenzo Stoakes</span>

<span style="font-family:'DogmaBold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#ffffff">N O T E</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">It is actually possible for distinct nodes and zones to overlap one another, for instance</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">in cases where access times for memory in the overlapping region are equivalent in</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">each node, however for the sake of brevity we will assume these ranges are distinct.</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura-Bold';font-size:11.95pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">2.1</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura-Bold';font-size:11.95pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">struct page</span>

<span style="font-family:'DogmaBold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#ffffff">N O T E</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Rather than confuse matters and include every permutation of kernel configuration</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">and platform we focus on modern 64-bit, little-endian architectures with sensible</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">configurations. This might seem like heresy, but trying to cover everything would</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">render this book unreadable and my sanity unknowable.</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">In total the size of the structure on a modern x86-64 system is 64 bytes</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">(the typical size of a L1 cache line) and is typically laid out in such a way that</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">it is accessed</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> contiguously</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> in memory meaning that</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> objects can be</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">accessed very efficiently.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Each</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> represents the smallest page size the kernel (and typ-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">ically the system) supports (e.g. for x86-64 this is 4 KiB), however physi-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">cally contiguous pages can be compounded together resulting in</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> compound</span>

<span style="font-family:'Futura-CondensedBold';font-size:8.97pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">8</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura';font-size:5.98pt;color:#000000">Chapter 2</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">In order to manage pages of memory we must store metadata about them—</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">flags to identify what characteristics the page has, reference count to deter-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">mine whether we can free the page or not and a whole host of other meta-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">data specific to how they are used.</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">The data type that encapsulates this data is</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> which, for mod-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">ern 64-bit systems contains:</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">• A</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> flags</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> field which specifies attributes of the page and additionally en-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">codes zone and optionally node information (it can also encode ‘section’</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">information under certain configuration options, this is out of scope at</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">this point.) set via</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> set_page_zone()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> set_page_node()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and accessed via</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">page_zonenum()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> page_to_nid()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">• A 40-byte</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> metadata union</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">, a union of a series of data structures which</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">varies depending on what the page is being used for. This is used to</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">store pertinent metadata to the page depending on type, or if used for</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">‘slab’ pages (see the slab chapter for more on this) the whole</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">is cast to a</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct slab</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> object, which shares</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> flags</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">,</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> _refcount</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> memcg_data</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">fields but overwrites the metadata union and</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> _mapcount</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">/</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">page_type</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> fields.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">• If not a slab page—a union of either a</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> _mapcount</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> variable (which should be</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">accessed via</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> page_mapcount()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">) counting page table mappings if the page is</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">mappable in userland (or a</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> page_type</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> field giving further details on the</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">page type.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">• A reference count</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> _refcount</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> field (which should be accessed via</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">page_ref_count()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">) used to determine if this page can be freed typically</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">incremented by</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> get_page()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and decremented by</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> put_page()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">• A</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> memcg_data</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> field used to store data pertinent to memory cgroups, typi-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">cally a pointer to a cgroup data structure.</span>

---

## Page 24

<span style="font-family:'Arial';font-size:8.00pt;color:#a3a3a3">The Linux Memory Manager (Early Access) © 2025 by Lorenzo Stoakes</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">pages</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> allocated as a block. In order to square this circle we designate the first</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> of a compound page a</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> head</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> page and the remainder</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> tail</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> pages.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Compound pages will always consist of a power-of-2 number of base</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">pages equal to 2</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:6.97pt;color:#000000">order</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> </span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">and referred to as ‘order-N’ pages, e.g. an order-0 page</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">is 2</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:6.97pt;color:#000000">0</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> </span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">= 1 base page in size, an order-1 page is 2</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:6.97pt;color:#000000">1</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> </span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">= 2 base pages in size, an</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">order-2 page is 2</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:6.97pt;color:#000000">2</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> </span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">= 4 base pages in size and so forth.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">To add to the confusion, it is possible to allocate higher order pages with-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">out them being compound – in which case it is assumed the owner of the</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">page simply knows which</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> represents the higher-order page. In</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">order to obtain a compound page, the</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> __GFP_COMP</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> flag must be set (more on</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">GFP flags later).</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">The terminology is confusing here – both higher order pages and base</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">pages are referred to simply as</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> pages</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">. A good rule of thumb is, unless quali-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">fied as a ‘compound’ page or an ‘order-N’ page, it is usually safe to assume</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">that the term ‘page’ refers to a page of base size, especially when expressed</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">as a unit e.g. ‘137 pages’.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Overall the philosophy of</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> is to utilise the space taken up by</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">each object as efficiently as possible, squeezing out the available space for</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">all its worth. As a result there is a heavy use of unions overloading the use</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">of each offset within the struct as well as the aforementioned casting of</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> to</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct slab</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> (this object is used for slab allocation, see the slab</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">chapter for more on this).</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Historically when a</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> has been referred to (for example</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">as a function parameter), it has not been possible to guarantee that it</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">wasn’t a tail page. The solution until recently has been to always invoke</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">compound_head()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> which, if it was indeed a tail page exchanged it for its head.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">However rather sensibly the kernel has moved towards explicitly indicat-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">ing that these parameters are</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> not</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> tail pages so that this uncertainty can be</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">eliminated. This is achieved by using the</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct folio</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> type which maps one-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">to-one to a</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> but is</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> always</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> either non-compound or a head page.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Helper functions exist to ease the transition as interfaces are updated, and</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">for the moment</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct folio</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> contains a top-level union with a</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> so</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">it is very easy to convert between the two. More on this later.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">After excising fields that aren’t relevant to a modern x86-64 system the</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">definition is as follows, as shown in Listing 2-1.</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">72</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">struct</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> page {</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">75</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Ita';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000">/*</span>

<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Ita';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000">* Five words (20/40 bytes) are available in this union.</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">79</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Ita';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000">* avoid collision and false-positive PageTail().</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">80</span>

<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Ita';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000">/* ... (metadata union) ... */</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">186</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">The</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> _struct_page_alignment</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> define specifies that the page should be</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">aligned to double system word size (e.g. 16 bytes for 64-bit systems) if</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">CONFIG_HAVE_ALIGNED_STRUCT_PAGE</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> is set which it typically will be on modern sys-</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">size for better performance. Ultimately for x86-64 and arm64 this should</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">have no impact as in both cases</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> will be of cache line size – i.e. 64</span>

<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:5.36pt;color:#000000">unsigned int</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:5.36pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000"> page_type</span>

<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.70pt;color:#000000">60</span>

<span style="font-family:'Futura-BookOblique';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000">Figure 2-2:</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Ita';font-size:7.20pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000"> struct page</span><span style="font-family:'Futura-BookOblique';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000"> layout for a typical 64-bit architecture</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura-CondensedBoldObli';font-size:11.95pt;font-weight:bold;font-style:italic;color:#000000">2.1.1</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura-CondensedBoldObli';font-size:11.95pt;font-weight:bold;font-style:italic;color:#000000">Metadata</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura-CondensedBold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">2.1.1.1</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura-CondensedBold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">Anonymous/page cache pages</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">If a page is either allocated as a simple ‘anonymous’ page (i.e. not tied to a</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">file and not used for any special purpose requiring more metadata) or is a</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">part of the page cache (a page containing data for a memory-mapped file,</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">either explicitly mapped in or cached automatically, see later chapter on this</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">topic) then the metadata union used is, as shown in Listing 2-3.</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> mapping</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – A rather deceptively typed and named field – it points to</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">a page cache-specific</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct address_space mapping</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> field if this page is</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">part of the page cache (as one might expect), however the lower 2 bits</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">are given over to flags and if the</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PAGE_MAPPING_ANON</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> flag is set</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> alone</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> it</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">will instead point to a</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct anon_vma</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> object (see later chapter on this</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">topic). If the page does not appear on LRU lists (termed ‘non-LRU’)</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">it may set the the</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PAGE_MAPPING_MOVABLE</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> flag in which case the mapping</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">points at a</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct movable_operations</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> object. Finally, if the flags are set to</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">PAGE_MAPPING_KSM</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> (a combination of the prior two) it points to a private</span>

<span style="font-family:'Futura-BookOblique';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000">Figure 2-3:</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Ita';font-size:7.20pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000"> Anonymous page/page cache</span><span style="font-family:'Futura-BookOblique';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000"> metadata union struct</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">KSM data structure. KSM is</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> Kernel Samepage Merging</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">, which allows for</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">All rather confusing!</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> index</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – If this page is within a page (or swap) cache this field indicates</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">the offset of this page within the mapped file.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> private</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – A field containing private data that the filesystem which owns</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">the page can use for its own purposes (see the</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PG_private</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> comment for</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">more details).</span>

<span style="font-family:'DogmaBold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#ffffff">N O T E</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">A list head is a structure containing pointers to previous and next nodes in a doubly-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">linked ring list, implemented neatly by keeping nodes within structures and using the</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">statically known offset of the entry from the start of the structure to be able to retrieve</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">node contents at compile-time, see</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Ita';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000"> include/linux/list.h</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> to see the implementation.</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">We examine this in graphical form in Figure 2-3.</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">8</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">12</span>

## Page 29

<span style="font-family:'Arial';font-size:8.00pt;color:#a3a3a3">The Linux Memory Manager (Early Access) © 2025 by Lorenzo Stoakes</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura-CondensedBold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">2.1.1.2</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura-CondensedBold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">Tail pages</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Tail page metadata is represented in a slightly less clear fashion – two unions</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">containing overlapping information from the following</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">s, as shown in</span>

<span style="font-family:'Futura-BookOblique';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000">Listing 2-4:</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> include/linux/mm_types.h:</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Ita';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000"> Tail page metadata union structs</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Every</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> tail page has the</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> compound_head</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> field set which is a pointer to the</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">head page with the lower bit additionally set (this is how we identify tail</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">pages via</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PageTail()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">). This is set by</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> set_compound_head()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">, as shown in Listing</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">2-5.</span>

## Page 30

<span style="font-family:'Arial';font-size:8.00pt;color:#a3a3a3">The Linux Memory Manager (Early Access) © 2025 by Lorenzo Stoakes</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Note that this sets the</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> mapping</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> field to the known ‘poisoned’ value</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">TAIL_MAPPING</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> to mark these pages as being tail pages to make them more eas-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">ily identifiable when debugging.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">The</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> first</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> tail page contains additional information on the compound</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">page (since a page is compound if it contains more than one of the mini-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">mum page size, we know for sure there will be at least one tail page to place</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">this in).</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">We set this additional data in</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> prep_compound_head()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> which is also in-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">voked by</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> prep_compound_page()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> which sets the</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> compound_dtor</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">,</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> compound_order</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">,</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">compound_mapcount</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">,</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> compound_pincount</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> compound_nr</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> fields as shown in Listing</span>

<span style="font-family:'Futura-BookOblique';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000">Listing 2-11:</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> include/linux/mm_types.h:</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Ita';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000"> compound_pincount_ptr()</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">The</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> order</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> referred to here defines the number of pages compounded</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">together – the number of base pages contained in a compound page is equal</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">to 2</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:6.97pt;color:#000000">order</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">. using a power-of-2 allows us to use a</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> buddy allocator</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> to efficiently</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">allocate (more on that later!) The maximum order is equal to</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> MAX_ORDER</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> - 1</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">(typically 10, i.e. 2</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:6.97pt;color:#000000">10</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> </span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">= 1024 pages, on x86-64 this is 4 MiB).</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">You can see that each field being set is offset by 1 from the head page –</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">confirming that this data is stored in the</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> first</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> tail page.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">We can see how these are invoked by</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> prep_compound_page()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> in Listing 2-12.</span>
