<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Here</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> __SetPageHead()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> sets a flag to indicate that the page is a head page,</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">before invoking the functions we have explored above. These flag options</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">are generated using macros, e.g.</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> __SETPAGEFLAG()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and ultimately set the</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> flags</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">field in the</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> object.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">The</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> deferred_list</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> field is used by the transparent huge page (see later</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">chapter on this topic) logic to store individual constituent pages for deferred</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">processing, typically accessed via</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> page_deferred_list()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Huge pages (page sizes larger than the smallest supported page size)</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">must consist of a compound page so we know will have at least two tail pages</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">and therefore can safely reference a second tail page, as shown in Listing 2-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">13.</span>

<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.70pt;color:#000000">44</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.70pt;color:#000000">48</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura-BookOblique';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000">Figure 2-4:</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Ita';font-size:7.20pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000"> Tail page</span><span style="font-family:'Futura-BookOblique';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000"> metadata union fields</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Reviewing what each field is used for:</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">294</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">static inline struct</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> list_head *</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">page_deferred_list</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">(</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">struct</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> page *page)</span>

<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:5.36pt;color:#000000">unsigned long</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:5.36pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000"> compound_head</span>

<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:5.36pt;color:#000000">struct list_head</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:5.36pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000"> deferred_list</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:6.30pt;color:#000000">First tail page</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:6.30pt;color:#000000">Second tail page (if huge)</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:6.30pt;color:#000000">All other tail pages</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> compound_head</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – Pointer to the</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> head page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> of the compound page with its</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">high bit set (e.g. if the head page resided at</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> 0xf00ba100</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> then this value</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">would be</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> 0xf00ba101</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and require the lower bit to be masked off). A com-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">mon task for a function that takes a</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> as an argument is to</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">check whether the page is in fact a tail page and in that case obtain its</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">head. This is achieved through the</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> compound_head()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> macro (more on</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">this later!) this field allows us to determine if a page is a tail page via</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">PageTail()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> or more generally compound via</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PageCompound()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">.</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">and these pages are ‘pinned’ in place (i.e. made such that they cannot</span>

---

## Page 34

<span style="font-family:'Arial';font-size:8.00pt;color:#a3a3a3">The Linux Memory Manager (Early Access) © 2025 by Lorenzo Stoakes</span>

<span style="font-family:'Futura-CondensedBold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">2.1.1.3</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura-CondensedBold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">Page table pages</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Page tables (see later chapter on this topic) require a lock to synchronise</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">changes, and typically it is efficient to ‘split’ these locks at the lowest two</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">page table levels (designated ‘</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">PTE</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">s’ and ‘</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">PMD</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">s’ – we go into more detail</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">on what these mean in the next chapter) so there are separate locks for each</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">individual page. Additionally there are some huge page and architecture-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">specific metadata that is convenient to store in the essentially ‘free’ data</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">store that is a</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> in use. Examining the struct as shown in Listing</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">2-16.</span>

<span style="font-family:'DogmaBold';font-size:9.96pt;font-weight:bold;color:#ffffff">N O T E</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Note as with the</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Ita';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000"> struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> code listing we are assuming</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Ita';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000"> ALLOC_SPLIT_PTLOCKS</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> is not</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">set which is the case for modern 64-bit architectures as this parameter is determined</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">by whether the spinlock size exceeds the number of bytes in an</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Ita';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000"> unsigned long</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> which</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">will not be the case unless lock debugging is configured.</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">154</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">struct</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> {</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Ita';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000">/* Page table pages */</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">155</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">unsigned long</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> _pt_pad_1;</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Ita';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000">/* compound_head */</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">156</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">pgtable_t</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> pmd_huge_pte;</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Ita';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000"> /* protected by page-&gt;ptl */</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">158</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">union</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> {</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">159</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">struct</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> mm_struct *pt_mm;</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Ita';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000"> /* x86 pgds only */</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">161</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">};</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">...</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">165</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">spinlock_t</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> ptl;</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">...</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">167</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">};</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Note that the padding in this struct ensures the tail page bit in</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">compound_head</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> is clear so</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PageTail()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> will return false, and as a non-tail page</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">efforts space is left to ensure the</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> mapping</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> field from the page cache struct is</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">null (you will note that the metadata union structs each go to pains to en-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">sure this is the case – the</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> will be zeroed other than fields in use).</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Similarly, where the</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> mapping</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> would be for the anonymous/page cache entry</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">is kept zeroed to avoid mistaking the page for either an anonymous or page</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">cache one.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">be moved or paged out, more on user pages and pinning later), this field</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">is used to store a precise count of the number of times the compound</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">page has been pinned.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> compound_nr</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – A field added for convenience in 64-bit architectures which</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">is equal to 2</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:5.93pt;color:#000000">compound_order</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> </span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">i.e. the number of base pages this compound</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">page occupies.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> deferred_list</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – As described previously, this is used as part of the trans-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">parent huge page functionality, see later chapter on this topic.</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">157</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">unsigned long</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> _pt_pad_2;</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Ita';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000">/* mapping */</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">160</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">atomic_t</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> pt_frag_refcount;</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Ita';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000"> /* powerpc */</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura-BookOblique';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000">Listing 2-16:</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> include/linux/mm_types.h:</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Ita';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000"> Page table metadata union struct</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> pmd_huge_pte</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – This is used by the transparent hugepage functionality</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">(see later chapter on this topic) to tie a potentially huge</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> PMD</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> to an un-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">derlying fallback</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> PTE</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">. Its type is</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> pgtable_t</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> which for</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> x86-64</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> arm64</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> is</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">typedef’d to a</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page*</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">. If</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> USE_SPLIT_PMD_PTLOCKS</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> is set (typically the</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">case, see below) then</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> pmd_huge_pte()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> references this field.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> pt_mm</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – This is used by the x86 architecture to store a pointer from the</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">PGD page table to its relevant</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct mm_struct</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> (more on this later!)</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> pt_frag_refcount</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – This is a PowerPC-specific field (for sake of brevity I</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">examine only x86-64 in this book).</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> ptl</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – This lock is used for</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> PTE</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> page tables when</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> USE_SPLIT_PTE_PTLOCKS</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">is set (when the</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> maximum</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> number of cores defined by</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> CONFIG_NR_CPUS</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">,</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">which typically defaults to at least 64, is greater than or equal to</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">CONFIG_SPLIT_PTLOCK_CPUS</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">, which typically defaults to 4, so this is almost</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">certainly the case for any modern system) and used for</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> PMD</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> page ta-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">bles when</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> USE_SPLIT_PMD_PTLOCKS</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> is set (when</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> USE_SPLIT_PTE_PTLOCKS</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">CONFIG_ARCH_ENABLE_SPLIT_PMD_PTLOCK</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> are set which is typically the case),</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">otherwise a shared lock is used.</span>

<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:5.36pt;color:#000000">pgtable_t</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:5.36pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000"> pmd_huge_pte</span>

## Page 39

<span style="font-family:'Arial';font-size:8.00pt;color:#a3a3a3">The Linux Memory Manager (Early Access) © 2025 by Lorenzo Stoakes</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura-CondensedBoldObli';font-size:11.95pt;font-weight:bold;font-style:italic;color:#000000">2.1.2</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura-CondensedBoldObli';font-size:11.95pt;font-weight:bold;font-style:italic;color:#000000">struct slab</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">The</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct slab</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> object is declared separately from</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and does not</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">form part of its metadata union but is however cast to/from it, converting</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">from pages to slabs via</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> page_slab()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and back again via</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> slab_page()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">. It is there-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">fore effectively a metadata union entry, though maintained in a separate</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">data structure and as per figure 2-2.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">This object is used to track state relating to the kernel</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> slab allocator</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">caching objects for allocation in this page, see later chapter on this topic.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">I won’t dwell too long on what each field refers to as going into detail on</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">this is better suited to the slab chapter however, briefly, each of the three dif-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">ferent slab allocators (SLAB, SLUB and SLOB) typically share the following</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">fields:</span>

<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">8</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Ita';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000">/* Reuses the bits in struct page */</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">9</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">struct</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> slab {</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">10</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">unsigned long</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> __page_flags;</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">11</span>

<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">union</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> {</span>

<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">struct</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> list_head slab_list;</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">27</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">struct</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> rcu_head rcu_head;</span>

<span style="font-family:'Futura-CondensedBold';font-size:8.97pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">24</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura';font-size:5.98pt;color:#000000">Chapter 2</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> slab_list</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – The doubly-linked list node that allows slab pages to be</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">placed on free lists as deemed appropriate by the specific slab algorithm</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">used. Alignment of this field ensures the lowest bit will be clear and so it</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">won’t be mistaken by</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PageTail()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> for a tail page.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> rcu_head</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – This forms the fundamental data structure permitting the</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">use of</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> Read, Copy, Update (RCU)</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> for</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct slab</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> objects. I will cover the</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">specifics of this in more detail in the slab chapter. Similar to</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> slab_list</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">alignment ensures this won’t be mistaken for a tail page.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> slab_cache</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – The slab cache object this particular slab belongs to. Note</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">that this coincides with the anonymous page/page cache</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> mapping</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> field so</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">we rely on alignment here to ensure the lower bits will not be set falsely</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">indicating an anonymous or movable page.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">We examine the</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct slab</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> data structure in Listing 2-19.</span>

## Page 41

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Note that the ‘active, per-CPU partial caches’ fields here are enabled by set-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">ting the</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> CONFIG_SLUB_CPU_PARTIAL</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> configuration option.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Briefly examining each SLUB-specific field:</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> next</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – (only if</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> CONFIG_SLUB_CPU_PARTIAL</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> is set) If the current slab object</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">only represents a partial portion of the overall cache, this points at the</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">next slab.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> slabs</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – (only if</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> CONFIG_SLUB_CPU_PARTIAL</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> is set) The number of slabs in this</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">particular cache.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> counters</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – This consists of the bitfields</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> inuse</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">,</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> objects</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> frozen</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">, with the</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">counters</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> variable provided for convenience to enable copying all of them</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">at once.</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> freelist</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – Thread-safe accessible list of free objects.</span>

<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">struct list_head</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:6.78pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000"> slab_list</span>

<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">long</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:6.78pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000"> units</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> units</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – If positive, indicates the size of this block, if negative indicates</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">the offset of the next block.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Page flags describing their attributes are kept in three separate fields in</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">:</span>

---

## Page 44

<span style="font-family:'Arial';font-size:8.00pt;color:#a3a3a3">The Linux Memory Manager (Early Access) © 2025 by Lorenzo Stoakes</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page-&gt;flags</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – This field specialises any of a large number of flags</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">each of which are defined in</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> enum pageflags</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">. There are 28 basic flags as</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">well as additional flags which overload these.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page-&gt;page_type</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – This field defines additional fields for non-slab,</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">non-user mappable pages, declared as preprocessor macros but still</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">maintaining the same</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PG_</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> prefix as</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> flags</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> fields.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page-&gt;mapping</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – The lower two bits of this field can be set to ei-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">ther</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PAGE_MAPPING_ANON</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">,</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PAGE_MAPPING_MOVABLE</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">, or the combination of both –</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">PAGE_MAPPING_KSM</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">. These indicate whether the page is anonymous, mov-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">able or part of the Kernel Samepage Merging (KSM) functionality.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">These of course are prefixed with the</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PAGE_MAPPING_</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> prefix.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">The majority of page flags and related functions are defined in the</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">include/linux/page-flags.h</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> header. Flags are accessed by test/set/clear func-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">tions of the form</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> xxxPageyyy</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">. The majority are generated by macros, but a</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">few which require special handling are manually declared. Regardless they</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">all follow the same naming convention:</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000"> Page</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">xxx</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – This is a boolean function that simply tests whether the flag</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">is set or not.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000"> SetPage</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">xxx</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – This sets the flag and guarantees this is done</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> atomically</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000"> __SetPage</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">xxx</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – This sets the flag but is not</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> guaranteed</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> to be atomic.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000"> TestSetPage</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">xxx</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – This sets the flag and returns the old state as a</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">boolean, guaranteed to be done atomically.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000"> ClearPage</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">xxx</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – This clears the flag and guarantees this is done atomi-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">cally.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000"> __ClearPage</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">xxx</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – This clears the flag but is not</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> guaranteed</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> to be atomic.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000"> TestClearPage</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">xxx</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Bol';font-size:8.47pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – This clears the flag and returns the old state as a</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">boolean, guaranteed to be done atomically.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">In most cases, flags specify a</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> policy</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> which performs a check on the page</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">and potentially transforms which page the flags are accessed on:</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PF_POISONED_CHECK</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – Checks whether the</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> flags</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> field is set to a known ‘poi-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">son’ value meaning that the flags are invalid via</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PagePoisoned()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">. This is</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">always</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> enforced and checked by</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> all</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> policies below in addition to their</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">own checks.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PF_ANY</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – Can be used on</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> any</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> page, regardless of whether it is compound,</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">head or tail.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PF_HEAD</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – Transform page to a head page if its compound or do nothing</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">if not via</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> compound_head()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> .</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PF_ONLY_HEAD</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> –</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> Always</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> check to ensure this isn’t a tail page.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PF_NO_TAIL</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – Check to ensure this is not a tail page if setting/clearing.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PF_NO_COMPOUND</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – Check to ensure it isn’t a compound page if setting/-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">clearing.</span>

<span style="font-family:'Futura';font-size:5.98pt;color:#000000">Physical Memory</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura-CondensedBold';font-size:8.97pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">29</span>

---

## Page 45

<span style="font-family:'Arial';font-size:8.00pt;color:#a3a3a3">The Linux Memory Manager (Early Access) © 2025 by Lorenzo Stoakes</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Note that these checks are performed via</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> VM_BUG_ON_PGFLAGS()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> which will</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">only do something meaningful at runtime if</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> CONFIG_DEBUG_VM_PGTABLE</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> is config-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">ured.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">We examine all available page flag helpers in Table 2-1.</span>

<span style="font-family:'Futura-CondensedBold';font-size:8.97pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">30</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura';font-size:5.98pt;color:#000000">Chapter 2</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PF_SECOND</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> –</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> Always</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> check to ensure it is a head page, accesses flags on</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">second page (i.e. first tail page).</span>

<span style="font-family:'Futura';font-size:5.98pt;color:#000000">Physical Memory</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura-CondensedBold';font-size:8.97pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">31</span>

---

## Page 47

<span style="font-family:'Arial';font-size:8.00pt;color:#a3a3a3">The Linux Memory Manager (Early Access) © 2025 by Lorenzo Stoakes</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">The</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PG_arch_1</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">,</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PG_arch_2</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PG_fscache</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> flags from</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> enum pageflags</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> do not</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">have functions associated with them so they were excluded from the pre-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">ceding table. Additionally, a number of these flags are dependent on config</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">options being set to be available.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">We will examine each flag individually, however before we do so let’s ex-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">amine the key</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct folio</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> data structure.</span>

<span style="font-family:'Futura-Bold';font-size:11.95pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">2.2</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura-Bold';font-size:11.95pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">struct folio</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">While compound pages are a useful abstraction they cause an unfortunate</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">ambiguity for any code working with a pointer to a</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – you might</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">always be dealing with an arbitrary tail page. This is a problem because com-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">pound page metadata is located either on the head page or one of the tail</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">pages immediately following it.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">As a result, any function that must process a</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> has historically</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">passed it through</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> compound_head()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> which takes a page as input and is guaran-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">teed to returns either the head page if it is compound or the page itself if it</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">is not.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">This is clearly suboptimal and results in functions being unintentionally</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">weakly typed – there is no way to know whether a function parameterised</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">by</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> is intended to interact with head (or non-compound) pages or</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">tail pages without examining the code carefully.</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">struct folio</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> addresses these shortcomings by explicitly</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> guaranteeing</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">that it is either non-compound or the head of a compound page. it is</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">binary-compatible with</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and can be used in place of it with the</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">use of some wrapper functions which translate between</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">struct folio</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> –</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> page_folio()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> folio_page()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">These wrapper functions are intended to be removed the kernel over</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">time as it moves towards using</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct folio</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">’s directly in more and more</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">places.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">The</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct folio</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> declaration also provides a wonderful description:</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">“A folio is a physically, virtually and logically contiguous set of bytes. It</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">is a power-of-two in size, and it is aligned to that same power-of-two. It is at</span>

<span style="font-family:'Futura-CondensedBold';font-size:8.97pt;font-weight:bold;color:#000000">32</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura';font-size:5.98pt;color:#000000">Chapter 2</span>

<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> (no symbol)</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – Denotes that the flag is stored in</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page-&gt;flags</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and the</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">function was generated by a macro.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'LMMathSymbols7-Regular';font-size:6.97pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000"> </span><span style="font-family:'LMMathSymbols7-Regular';font-size:6.97pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000">∗</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">– Denotes that the flag is stored in</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page-&gt;page_type</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and the func-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">tion was generated by a macro.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'LMMathSymbols7-Regular';font-size:6.97pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000"> </span><span style="font-family:'LMMathSymbols7-Regular';font-size:6.97pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000">∗∗</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">– Denotes that the function refers to a</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page-&gt;flags</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> flag but is</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">implemented manually rather than being generated by a macro.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'LMMathSymbols10-Regular';font-size:9.96pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000"> †</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – Denotes that the flag is stored in</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page-&gt;mapping</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and is imple-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">mented manually rather than being generated by a macro.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'LMMathSymbols10-Regular';font-size:9.96pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000"> ‡</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> – Denotes that the function is implemented manually but has no flag</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">associated with it but follows the same naming convention.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">•</span><span style="font-family:'LMMathSymbols10-Regular';font-size:9.96pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000"> ←</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">– Denotes a flag that overloads an existing flag rather than having its</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">own bit assigned.</span>

## Page 48

<span style="font-family:'Arial';font-size:8.00pt;color:#a3a3a3">The Linux Memory Manager (Early Access) © 2025 by Lorenzo Stoakes</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">least as large as</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PAGE_SIZE</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">. If it is in the page cache, it is at a file offset which</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">is a multiple of that power-of-two. It may be mapped into userspace at an</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">address which is at an arbitrary page offset, but its kernel virtual address is</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">aligned to its size.”</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">We will examine allocation of physical memory later in this chapter and</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">virtual memory in the next, but suffice to say the two are aligned precisely as</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">described here.</span>

<span style="font-family:'Futura-BookOblique';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000">Listing 2-22:</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> include/linux/page-flags.h:</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Ita';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000"> folio_page()</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">As the transition from page to folio can be taken from any base page</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">page_folio()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> implicitly applies</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> _compound_head()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> which is the untyped version</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">of</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> compound_head()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">, and thus this function need only be parameterised only by</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">the page.</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">folio_page()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> is a little trickier, as the caller may either wish to access the</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">head page or a specific tail page. This is addressed by providing an index</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">parameter so the caller can indicate which page is required.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">As some flags are located on tail pages, it is convenient to have a helper</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">function which retrieves page flags located on a specific page, which is pro-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">vided by</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> folio_flags()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> as shown in Listing 2-23.</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:6.78pt;color:#000000">315</span>

## Page 52

<span style="font-family:'Arial';font-size:8.00pt;color:#a3a3a3">The Linux Memory Manager (Early Access) © 2025 by Lorenzo Stoakes</span>
<span style="font-family:'Futura-BookOblique';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000">Listing 2-23:</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> include/linux/page-flags.h:</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Ita';font-size:8.47pt;font-style:italic;color:#000000"> folio_flags()</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Which does what you’d expect, with debug assertions to check sanity (en-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">abled only if</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> CONFIG_DEBUG_VM_PGTABLE</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> is set). The assertions ensure that the</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">folio page isn’t a tail page (this would imply something had gone</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-RomanIt';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> horribly</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">wrong) and if a tail page is being tested, that the head page has</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> PG_head</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> set</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">asserting that this is a compound page under examination.</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">The</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct folio</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> fields have the same meaning as</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and sim-</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">ilarly</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> _mapcount</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> _refcount</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> fields should not be accessed directly but via</span>
<span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000">folio_mapcount()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> folio_ref_count()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> respectively (though the reference</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">count will typically be handled by</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> folio_get()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000"> and</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> folio_put()</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">).</span>
<span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">Flag helpers are generated in the same way they are for</span><span style="font-family:'TheSansMonoCondensed-Pla';font-size:8.47pt;color:#000000"> struct page</span><span style="font-family:'NewBaskervilleEF-Roman';font-size:9.96pt;color:#000000">’s</span>
